In graph theory, a graph is bipartite if its vertices can be divided into two disjoint sets such that no two graph vertices within the same set are adjacent. In this case, adjacency is based on diagonal moves. If two squares are diagonally adjacent, their (i + j) sums differ by 0 or 2. For example, moving from (0,1) to (1,2): sum increases by 2 (1 to 3). Moving from (1,2) to (2,3): sum increases by 2 (3 to 5). Moving from (2,3) to (3,4): sum increases by 2 (5 to 7). Moving from (3,4) to (4,5): sum increases by 2 (7 to 9). Moving from (4,5) to (5,6): sum increases by 2 (9 to 11). Moving from (5,6) to (6,5): sum stays the same (11). Moving from (6,5) to (7,4): sum stays the same (11). So, in this case, parity (mod 4) of the sum is:1 mod 4, 3 mod 4, 1 mod 4, 3 mod 4, 1 mod 4, 3 mod 4, 3 mod 4, 3 mod 4.So, the parity alternates until the last two steps, where it stays the same. Therefore, the graph is not bipartite because you can have edges that preserve the parity (mod 4). For example, moving from (5,6) to (6,5): sum remains 11, which is 3 mod 4. Therefore, such a move connects two nodes of the same parity, implying the graph is not bipartite. Hence, previous assumption is wrong.Therefore, the graph of white squares with diagonal adjacency is not bipartite, which allows for paths of various lengths and parities. :Solve As shown in Figure 17-3, the surface of the tetrahedron is cut along the side edge V A, and its unfolded diagram is shown in Figure 17-4. The perimeter of triangle A E D is minimized if and only if points D, E lie on line A A^{prime}. Let angle B V C=alpha, then angle A V A^{prime}=3 alpha . cos 3 alpha=4 cos ^{3} alpha-3 cos alphaIn triangle V B C, by the cosine rule, we get cos alpha=frac{V B^{2}+V C^{2}-B C^{2}}{2 cdot V B cdot V C}=frac{2 times 8^{2}-4^{2}}{2 times 8^{2}}=frac{7}{8}Therefore, cos 3 alpha=4 timesleft(frac{7}{8}right)^{3}-3 times frac{7}{8}=frac{7}{2^{7}}In triangle A V A^{prime}, by the cosine rule, we getA A^{prime}=sqrt{V A^{2}+V A^{prime 2}-2 V A cdot V A^{prime} cdot cos 3 alpha}=sqrt{8^{2}+8^{2}-2 cdot 8 cdot 8 cdot frac{7}{2^{7}}}=11Thus, the minimum perimeter of triangle A D E is 11.

We need to find the angle of inclination ( theta ) of the line ( l ) given ( frac{1}{|AF|} - frac{1}{|BF|} = frac{1}{2} ).1. Equation of the Line: The line passing through ( F(1, 0) ) with slope ( tan theta ) can be parametrized as ( x = 1 + t cos theta ) and ( y = t sin theta ).2. Intersection with Parabola: Substituting ( x ) and ( y ) into the parabola equation ( y^2 = 4x ): [ (t sin theta)^2 = 4(1 + t cos theta) ] Simplifying, we get the quadratic equation: [ t^2 sin^2 theta - 4t cos theta - 4 = 0 ]3. Solving the Quadratic Equation: The roots ( t_1 ) and ( t_2 ) are: [ t_1 = frac{2(cos theta + 1)}{sin^2 theta}, quad t_2 = frac{2(cos theta - 1)}{sin^2 theta} ] The distances ( |AF| ) and ( |BF| ) are ( |t_1| ) and ( |t_2| ).4. Distances Calculation: [ |AF| = frac{2(1 + cos theta)}{sin^2 theta}, quad |BF| = frac{2(1 - cos theta)}{sin^2 theta} ]5. Reciprocal Distances: [ frac{1}{|AF|} - frac{1}{|BF|} = frac{sin^2 theta}{2(1 + cos theta)} - frac{sin^2 theta}{2(1 - cos theta)} ] Simplifying using ( sin^2 theta = 1 - cos^2 theta ): [ frac{1 - cos theta}{2} - frac{1 + cos theta}{2} = -cos theta ] Given ( -cos theta = frac{1}{2} ), we find ( cos theta = -frac{1}{2} ), but this is not possible for ( 0 < theta < frac{pi}{2} ).6. Parametric Approach: Using parametric equations of the parabola ( (t^2, 2t) ) and the focal chord property ( ts = -1 ), we find the distances ( |AF| ) and ( |BF| ): [ |AF| = t^2 + 1, quad |BF| = frac{t^2 + 1}{t^2} ] Solving ( frac{1 - t^2}{1 + t^2} = frac{1}{2} ), we get ( t = pm frac{1}{sqrt{3}} ).7. Slope Calculation: For ( t = -frac{1}{sqrt{3}} ), the slope is ( sqrt{3} ), corresponding to ( theta = frac{pi}{3} ).Thus, the angle of inclination ( theta ) is (boxed{B}).,<think>Okay, let's try to tackle this problem step by step. The condition given is ( frac{1}{|AF|} - frac{1}{|BF|} = frac{1}{2} ). We need to find the angle of inclination ( theta ) of the line ( l ).1. Parametric Equations Approach: - For the parabola ( y^2 = 4x ), parametric coordinates are ( (t^2, 2t) ). - If points ( A ) and ( B ) correspond to parameters ( t_1 ) and ( t_2 ), the line passing through ( F(1, 0) ) must satisfy the condition ( t_1 t_2 = -1 ) (known property of focal chords).2. Distance Calculation: - Distances ( |AF| ) and ( |BF| ) are calculated as ( t_1^2 + 1 ) and ( frac{t_1^2 + 1}{t_1^2} ) respectively. - Using the given condition ( frac{1}{|AF|} - frac{1}{|BF|} = frac{1}{2} ), we solve for ( t_1 ): [ frac{1 - t_1^2}{t_1^2 + 1} = frac{1}{2} ] - Solving this, we find ( t_1 = pm frac{1}{sqrt{3}} ).3. Slope Calculation: - For ( t_1 = -frac{1}{sqrt{3}} ), the corresponding ( t_2 = sqrt{3} ). - The slope of the line through points ( A ) and ( B ) is ( frac{2}{t_1 + t_2} = sqrt{3} ), leading to ( tan theta = sqrt{3} ).4. Angle Determination: - The angle ( theta ) with ( tan theta = sqrt{3} ) is ( frac{pi}{3} ).Thus, the angle of inclination ( theta ) is (boxed{B}).]

:We have two methods to solve this problem:Method 1: The slope k of line AB exists since it goes through the parabola. Let the points be A(x_1,y_1) and B(x_2,y_2) and the focus be F(1,0). The equation of line AB is given by y=k(x-1).Equating this to the parabola's equation, we have y^2=4x, which gives us:begin{cases} y=k(x-1) y^2=4x end{cases}Simplifying, we get k^2x^2 - 2(k^2+2)x + k^2 = 0.Now, by applying Vieta's formulas, we find:x_1 + x_2 = frac{2(k^2+2)}{k^2} quad text{and} quad x_1x_2 = 1.Then, we can calculate:x_2 - x_1 = sqrt{(x_1 + x_2)^2 - 4x_1x_2} = frac{4sqrt{1+k^2}}{k^2}.Given dfrac{1}{|AF|} - dfrac{1}{|BF|} = dfrac{1}{x_1 + 1} - dfrac{1}{x_2 + 1} = dfrac{x_2 - x_1}{x_1x_2 + (x_1 + x_2) + 1} = dfrac{sqrt{1+k^2}}{1+k^2} = dfrac{1}{2}, we solve for k to get k = sqrt{3} or k = -sqrt{3}.Since 0 < theta < dfrac{pi}{2}, we choose k = sqrt{3}.Therefore, theta = dfrac{pi}{3}.Thus, the correct choice is boxed{B}.Method 2: Using the properties of a parabola's focal chord, we know that dfrac{1}{|AF|} + dfrac{1}{|BF|} = dfrac{p}{2} = 1, where p is the distance from the focus to the directrix, which is equal to 2 for our parabola y^2 = 4x. Using the condition dfrac{1}{|AF|} - dfrac{1}{|BF|} = dfrac{1}{2}, we can solve to find |AF| = dfrac{4}{3} and |BF| = 4. Therefore, |AB| = |AF|+|BF| = dfrac{16}{3} = dfrac{2p}{sin^2alpha} = dfrac{4}{sin^2alpha}. Solving for sinalpha gives us sinalpha = dfrac{sqrt{3}}{2}, and since 0 < theta < dfrac{pi}{2}, we have theta = dfrac{pi}{3}.Hence, the answer is boxed{B}.Method 1 establishes the equation of line AB and substitutes it in the equation of the parabola. Then, using Vieta's formulas, we find the differences x_2-x_1. We use properties of the parabola to find the values for |AF|, |BF|, and eventually the slope k, from which we calculate the angle theta. Method 2 uses the property of a parabola pertaining to the focal chord (i.e., the sum of reciprocals from the ends of a chord passing through the focus is constant) and the given condition to find |AF|, |BF|, and |AB|. Knowing |AB| = dfrac{2p}{sin^2alpha}, we can solve for the angle of inclination theta.The problem assesses the simple geometric properties of a parabola and the relationship between a line and a parabola, as well as computational ability. It is considered a medium-level question.
